## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (continuous-time population dynamics / demographic ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target is dP_dt, the time-derivative of population size P(t), which is the standard setup for continuous-time population growth models in ecology. Typical relationships encode per-capita growth, density dependence (crowding), Allee effects at low density, harvesting, and time-varying (seasonal or trending) growth rates via explicit dependence on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian exponential growth (constant per-capita rate): dP_dt = c0 * P
- Exponential growth with net immigration/emigration (source term): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1
- Density-independent forcing plus crowding (quadratic self-limitation): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (typically c1 < 0)
- Logistic ODE (linear density dependence via carrying capacity): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)
- Theta-logistic / generalized logistic (nonlinear density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2)
- Gompertz growth ODE (logarithmic density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)
- Richards-type generalized logistic (shape parameter on saturation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)
- Strong Allee effect with upper density limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P)
- Weak Allee effect (depressed growth at low P without negative growth): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P + 1)
- Logistic with proportional harvest (exploitation mortality): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P
- Logistic with constant-yield harvest (quota removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2
- Logistic with saturating harvest (effort-limited removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (1 + c3 * P)
- Seasonally forced per-capita rate (periodic environment): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P
- Time-trending per-capita rate (gradual environmental change): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If (dP_dt) / P is approximately constant across P, the process is close to exponential growth: dP_dt ∝ P.
- If dP_dt vs P is concave-down with a single positive peak and crosses zero at a positive P, a logistic-type term P*(1 - c*P) is suggested.
- If the per-capita growth (dP_dt)/P decreases roughly linearly with P, use linear density dependence (logistic); if it decreases nonlinearly, use theta-logistic P*(1 - c*P^theta).
- If growth slows in proportion to log(K/P) (per-capita growth declines approximately with log P), Gompertz form P*log(c/P) is indicated.
- If dP_dt is negative at low P but positive at intermediate P, include an Allee factor (c*P - 1) multiplying P to create a low-density threshold.
- If high-P equilibria shift downward without changing low-P behavior much, consider adding harvest terms: constant (−c) or proportional (−c*P).
- If removal appears to level off at high P (limited harvesting capacity), use a saturating harvest term like P/(1 + c*P).
- If growth rate exhibits periodic variation over time at similar P, include explicit seasonality in coefficients via sin(c*t + phase).
- If long-term acceleration/deceleration occurs over t (even at similar P), let the per-capita rate be a low-order function of time, e.g., (c0 + c1*t) or exp(c*t) multiplying P.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG7)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P**c9
Candidate formulas: 82

Let \(A=0.7213553457664288\), \(a=6.6511035054181695\), \(b=13.538092585698905\).  
GT:
\[
A(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P + A(1-P/b)P + A P^{1/3}.
\]
Combine the first two terms:
\[
A(1-P/b)P\big[(-1+P/a)+1\big] + A P^{1/3}
= A(1-P/b)P(P/a) + A P^{1/3}.
\]
So
\[
\text{GT}= A\left(\frac{P^2}{a} - \frac{P^3}{ab}\right) + A P^{1/3}.
\]
This is exactly a polynomial in \(P\) with only \(P^{1/3}, P^2, P^3\) terms and **no** \(P^1\) term, no constant term, and no \(t\)-dependence.

Numerically the coefficients are fixed:
- \(P^{1/3}\): \(A\)
- \(P^2\): \(A/a\)
- \(P^3\): \(-A/(ab)\)

Now check candidates: a candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by setting its free constants) to
\[
c_{1/3}P^{1/3} + c_2 P^2 + c_3 P^3
\]
with the three coefficients set to the GT values, and all other terms eliminated.

---

### 1
Has \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^3\), \(P^2\) (twice), plus constant \(c4\) and a \(t\)-dependent cosine product. Set cosine amplitude \(c5=0\) and constant \(c4=0\). Then choose \(c0=A\), \(c1=-A/(ab)\), and \(c2+c3=A/a\). **Matches.**

### 2
Includes \(P\) term, \(P^{c4}\) term, and \(t\)-dependent log*cos. You can set the log*cos coefficient \(c6=0\), set \(c3=0\) to remove \(P\), and set \(c5=0\) to remove \(P^{c4}\). Then it has \(P^3\) and \(P^2\) but **no \(P^{1/3}\)**. Cannot create \(P^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 3
Has \(P^{1/3}, P^3, P^2\) plus \(P\) term, \(t\)-dependent \(P\sin(\cdot)\), and constant. Set \(c5=0\) (remove sine term), \(c8=0\), \(c4=0\). Then choose \(c0=A\), \(c1=-A/(ab)\), \(c2+c3=A/a\). **Matches.**

### 4
Has \(P^{1/3}, P^3, P^2\) plus constant and \(t\)-dependent sine. Set \(c5=0\), \(c4=0\). Then set \(c0=A\), \(c1=-A/(ab)\), \(c2+c3=A/a\). **Matches.**

### 5
Has extra rational-in-\(t\) terms \(P*c4/(c5 t+c6)\) and \(c8/(c5 t+c6)\) plus constants. Only way to remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\) is set \(c4=0\) and \(c8=0\). Also set constant \(c7=0\). Then it reduces to the same \(P^{1/3},P^3,P^2\) structure; choose coefficients as above. **Matches.**

### 6
Contains \(P^{c4} \exp(P c6)\) which cannot equal a polynomial for all \(P\) unless its coefficient is zero. Set \(c5=0\) to remove it, set constant \(c7=0\). Then again choose \(c0=A\), \(c1=-A/(ab)\), \(c2+c3=A/a\). **Matches.**

### 11
Only integer-power terms: \(P^3\), \(P^2\), and \(P^{1+c3}\), \(P^{1+c5}\), \(P\). No \(P^{1/3}\) possible because all terms are \(P^k\) with \(k\ge 1\) (unless you force exponents to make \(P^{1/3}\), but they are multiplied by an extra \(P\): \(P*P^{c3}=P^{1+c3}\). Setting \(1+c3=1/3\) gives \(c3=-2/3\), possible, but then you still also need \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) with correct coefficients and must eliminate other terms. However you would then have a \(P^{1/3}\) term but **it is not of the form \(P^{1/3}\) alone; it’s fine actually**. Yet GT also needs \(P^2\) and \(P^3\). Candidate has \(P^3 c0\) and \(P^2(c1+c2)\). You can set one of the \(P^{1/3}\) terms via \(c3=-2/3\) and set the other \(P^{1+c5}\) term to vanish by \(c6=0\), and set \(P*c7\) to vanish by \(c7=0\). Then it becomes \(P^{1/3}c4 + P^2(\cdot)+P^3(\cdot)\). So it *can* match by choosing \(c4=A\), etc. **Matches.**

### 12
Has \(P*c4*(P*c5)^{c6}=c4 c5^{c6} P^{1+c6}\) plus \(P*c7\) and constant. You can set \(c7=0\), \(c8=0\). To avoid introducing an unwanted extra power besides \(1/3,2,3\), you’d need either set \(c4=0\) (remove it) or force \(1+c6\in\{1/3,2,3\}\). But you already have \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P^3\) available; easiest is set \(c4=0\). Then match coefficients. **Matches.**

### 13

### 14
All terms share denominator \(P^{c1}+c2\): rational function, not a polynomial unless denominator is constant. Denominator constant requires \(c1=0\) so \(P^{c1}=1\), giving constant denom \(1+c2\). Then expression becomes linear combination of \(P, P^{c3}, P^{c5}, P^{c7}\) (scaled). You could set exponents to \(1/3,2,3\) and zero out unwanted ones. But there is an unavoidable \(P\) term unless \(c0=0\). That’s fine (set \(c0=0\)). Then choose \(c3=1/3\), \(c5=2\), \(c7=3\) with appropriate coefficients and scaling by \(1/(1+c2)\). Yes. **Matches.**

### 15

## Simplifying the GT

GT: `0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P**0.333333333333333`

Let me denote `a = 0.7213553457664288`, `b = 6.6511035054181695`, `d = 13.538092585698905`.

First term: `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`
Second term: `a*(1 - P/d)*P`
Third term: `a*P^(1/3)`

Combine first two terms: `a*(1 - P/d)*P * [(-1 + P/b) + 1] = a*(1 - P/d)*P * (P/b)`
= `a*P²/b * (1 - P/d)`
= `a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d)`

So GT = `a*P^(1/3) + a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d)`

Computing constants:
- Coefficient of P^(1/3): `a ≈ 0.7214`
- Coefficient of P²: `a/b ≈ 0.7214/6.6511 ≈ 0.10846`
- Coefficient of P³: `-a/(b*d) ≈ -0.7214/(6.6511*13.5381) ≈ -0.008011`

**GT simplified: `c*P^(1/3) + d*P² + e*P³`** where c, d, e are specific constants.

This is a function of P only (no t dependence).

Now I check each candidate for structural match: needs P^(1/3), P², P³ terms only (no other basis functions that can't be zeroed out).

For candidates with `t` dependence: the coefficient of any `t`-dependent term must be settable to 0.

For candidates that are purely `P^(1/3) + P³ + P²` (possibly with redundant P² terms that merge, and constant terms that can be set to 0):

Let me systematically check:

**Candidates with the form P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2 + P²*c3 + [extra terms]:**

The base `P^(1/3) + P³ + P²` matches GT structure (c2+c3 gives one P² coefficient).

- **Candidate 1**: Extra: `c4 + c5*cos(P*c6)*cos(c7*t)` — cos(P*c6) can't be zeroed without zeroing c5, leaving constant c4. Setting c4=0 gives GT form. But wait, can we set c5=0 and c4=0? Yes! Then it's P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*(c2+c3). **MATCH**

Wait, but GT has no constant term. Let me recheck: GT = a*P^(1/3) + (a/b)*P² - (a/(bd))*P³. No constant. So c4=0, c5=0 works.

Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]
